Default is 1.\n1447:     bias : bool, optional\n1448:         If False, then the skewness and kurtosis calculations are corrected\n1449:         for statistical bias.\n1450:     nan_policy : {'propagate', 'raise', 'omit'}, optional\n1451:         Defines how to handle when input contains nan.\n1452:         The following options are available (default is 'propagate'):\n1453: \n1454:         * 'propagate': returns nan\n1455:         * 'raise': throws an error\n1456:         * 'omit': performs the calculations ignoring nan values\n1457: \n1458:     Returns\n1459:     -------\n1460:     nobs : int or ndarray of ints\n1461:         Number of observations (length of data along `axis`).\n1462:         When 'omit' is chosen as nan_policy, the length along each axis\n1463:         slice is counted separately.\n1464:     minmax: tuple of ndarrays or floats\n1465:         Minimum and maximum value of `a` along the given axis.\n1466:     mean : ndarray or float\n1467:         Arithmetic mean of `a` along the given axis.\n1468:     variance : ndarray or float\n1469:         Unbiased variance of `a` along the given axis; denominator is number\n1470:         of observations minus one.\n1471:     skewness : ndarray or float\n1472:         Skewness of `a` along the given axis, based on moment calculations\n1473:         with denominator equal to the number of observations, i.e. no degrees\n1474:         of freedom correction.\n1475:     kurtosis : ndarray or float\n1476:         Kurtosis (Fisher) of `a` along the given axis.  The kurtosis is\n1477:         normalized so that it is zero for the normal distribution.  No\n1478:         degrees of freedom are used.\n1479: \n1480:     Raises\n1481:     ------\n1482:     ValueError\n1483:         If size of `a` is 0.\n1484: \n1485:     See Also\n1486:     --------\n1487:     skew, kurtosis\n1488: \n1489:     Examples\n1490:     --------\n1491:     >>> import numpy as np\n1492:     >>> from scipy import stats\n1493:     >>> a = np.arange(10)\n1494:     >>> stats.describe(a)\n1495:     DescribeResult(nobs=10, minmax=(0, 9), mean=4.5,\n1496:                    variance=9.166666666666666, skewness=0.0,\n1497:                    kurtosis=-1.2242424242424244)\n1498:     >>> b = [[1, 2], [3, 4]]\n1499:     >>> stats.describe(b)\n1500:     DescribeResult(nobs=2, minmax=(array([1, 2]), array([3, 4])),\n1501:                    mean=array([2., 3.]), variance=array([2., 2.]),\n1502:                    skewness=array([0., 0.]), kurtosis=array([-2., -2.]))\n1503: \n1504:     \"\"\"\n1505:     xp = array_namespace(a)\n1506:     a, axis = _chk_asarray(a, axis, xp=xp)\n1507: \n1508:     contains_nan, nan_policy = _contains_nan(a, nan_policy)\n1509: \n1510:     if contains_nan and nan_policy == 'omit':\n1511:         # only NumPy gets here; `_contains_nan` raises error for the rest\n1512:         a = ma.masked_invalid(a)\n1513:         return mstats_basic.describe(a, axis, ddof, bias)\n1514: \n1515:     if xp_size(a) == 0:\n1516:         raise ValueError(\"The input must not be empty.\")\n1517: \n1518:     n = a.shape[axis]\n1519:     mm = (xp.min(a, axis=axis), xp.max(a, axis=axis))\n1520:     m = xp.mean(a, axis=axis)\n1521:     v = _var(a, axis=axis, ddof=ddof, xp=xp)\n1522:     sk = skew(a, axis, bias=bias)\n1523:     kurt = kurtosis(a, axis, bias=bias)\n1524: \n1525:     return DescribeResult(n, mm, m, v, sk, kurt)\n1526: \n1527: #####################################\n1528: #         NORMALITY TESTS           #\n1529: #####################################\n1530: \n1531: \n1532: def _get_pvalue(statistic, distribution, alternative, symmetric=True, xp=None):\n1533:     \"\"\"Get p-value given the statistic, (continuous) distribution, and alternative\"\"\"\n1534:     xp = array_namespace(statistic) if xp is None else xp\n1535: \n1536:     if alternative == 'less':\n1537:         pvalue = distribution.cdf(statistic)\n1538:     elif alternative == 'greater':\n1539:         pvalue = distribution.sf(statistic)\n1540:     elif alternative == 'two-sided':\n1541:         pvalue = 2 * (distribution.sf(xp.abs(statistic)) if symmetric\n1542:                       else xp.minimum(distribution.cdf(statistic),\n1543:                                       distribution.sf(statistic)))\n1544:     else:\n1545:         message = \"`alternative` must be 'less', 'greater', or 'two-sided'.\"\n1546:         raise ValueError(message)\n1547: \n1548:     return pvalue\n1549: \n1550: \n1551: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/scipy--v1.15.1@17b82484a2e4fae7b5e6d5fc16629ecc5cbd0495/-/blob/scipy/stats/_stats_py.py%3FL1435-1550"}}}
